## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Materials Science / Solid Mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models constitutive relationships in solid mechanics, specifically predicting mechanical stress (sigma) as a function of applied strain (epsilon) and temperature (T). It captures fundamental material behaviors such as elastic deformation, plastic strain hardening, thermal softening, and thermo-mechanical coupling.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hookean elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic deformation regime)
- Temperature-modulated stiffness: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (thermal dependence of Young's modulus)
- Hollomon strain hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (power-law plastic deformation)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (dislocation density saturation)
- Modified Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (initial yield stress plus strain hardening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 (accounts for pre-strain or initial yield offset)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (strain hardening coupled with thermal softening)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon) * (1 + c2 * T) (linear degradation of flow stress with temperature)
- Polynomial thermo-mechanical coupling: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (low-order coupled expansion for small deformations)
- Bilinear elastic-plastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * Max(epsilon - c2, 0) (two-stage deformation with distinct elastic and plastic moduli)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic-plastic transition → Bilinear or piecewise change in slope at a critical strain value, often modeled with Max(epsilon - c, 0) or smooth step functions
- Strain hardening behavior → Sublinear power-law scaling epsilon**c (0 < c < 1) indicating decreasing incremental stiffness with accumulated deformation
- Thermal softening effect → Negative temperature coefficient in multiplicative or exponential terms, e.g., (1 + c*T) with c < 0 or exp(c*T), reflecting strength degradation at elevated temperatures
- Dislocation saturation → Asymptotic approach to a flow stress limit, mathematically represented by (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or bounded functions like tanh(c*epsilon)
- Temperature-dependent modulus → Affine shift in the stress-strain slope expressed as (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon, capturing thermal expansion and phonon scattering effects
- Pre-strain/yield offset → Horizontal shift in the strain axis (epsilon + c) or additive constant yield term c0 + f(epsilon), accounting for initial dislocation structures or cold working
- Thermo-mechanical cross-coupling → Product term epsilon * T representing thermal strain contributions or temperature-modulated hardening rates in polycrystalline materials

### Analysis of Candidates vs Ground Truth

**Ground Truth (GT) Structure:**
`GT = c0*epsilon**3 - c2*(T - c3) + c4*(T - c5)*log(epsilon + 1)`
Expanding and grouping by basis functions:
`GT = c0*epsilon**3 + T*(c4*log(epsilon + 1) - c2) + c3*(c2 - c4*log(epsilon + 1))`
The GT is a linear combination of exactly five linearly independent basis functions:
1. `epsilon**3` (cubic polynomial in epsilon)
2. `T` (linear in T)
3. `1` (constant)
4. `T*log(epsilon + 1)` (product of T and log)
5. `log(epsilon + 1)` (logarithmic in epsilon)

**Candidate Evaluation:**
- **Basis Function Mismatch:** The GT strictly requires an `epsilon**3` term and a `T*log(epsilon + 1)` term. 
- **Polynomial/Logarithmic Independence:** Exponential (`exp`), trigonometric (`sin`, `cos`), square root (`sqrt`), and rational functions are linearly independent from polynomials and logarithms. They cannot algebraically simplify to `epsilon**3` or `T*log(epsilon+1)` under any constant assignment.
- **Candidate Scan:** 
  - Candidates 1-18, 22, 25-26, 28-30, 32-33, 35-36, 39, 41-45, 47-48 contain `exp`, `sin`, `cos`, `sqrt`, or `1/T` terms, which are absent in the GT. Even if their coefficients are zeroed, the remaining terms lack `epsilon**3` and `T*log(epsilon+1)`.
  - Candidates 19, 20, 27, 31, 34, 38, 40, 46 are purely rational functions. Rational functions cannot represent logarithmic terms exactly.
  - Candidates 21, 23, 24, 49, 50 are rational functions combined with `exp` terms. They lack the required polynomial and logarithmic basis.
  - Candidates 17, 37, 51 contain `exp(T*c)*log(...)` terms. `exp(T*c)` is exponentially independent from the linear `T` required in the GT. Setting `c=0` reduces them to `log(...)`, losing the `T` multiplier.
  - Candidate 15 has `epsilon*log(epsilon+1)`, which multiplies `epsilon` instead of `T`.
  - Candidate 25 has `epsilon**2`, not `epsilon**3`.
  - No candidate contains `epsilon**3` or `T*log(epsilon+1)`.

Since strict algebraic equivalence requires matching basis functions across the continuous domain, and no candidate contains the necessary `epsilon**3` or `T*log(epsilon+1)` structures, all candidates fail to match the Ground Truth.
